  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_44a9bead-175b-4eaf-b31d-7c4519bb9a8d'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText13850414628721051077" style="display:none"><i>The darker the sky, the brighter the stars.</i><br /><br />In a land on the brink of war, Shahrzad is forced from the arms of her beloved husband, the Caliph of Khorasan. She once thought Khalid a monster‚Äîa merciless killer of wives, responsible for immeasurable heartache and pain‚Äîbut as she unraveled his secrets, she found instead an extraordinary man and a love she could not deny. Still, a curse threatens to keep Shazi and Khalid apart forever.<br /><br />Now she‚Äôs reunited with her family, who have found refuge in the desert, where a deadly force is gathering against Khalid‚Äîa force set on destroying his empire and commanded by Shazi‚Äôs spurned childhood sweetheart. Trapped between loyalties to those she loves, the only thing Shazi can do is act. Using the burgeoning magic within her as a guide, she strikes out on her own to end both this terrible curse and the brewing war once and for all. But to do it, she must evade enemies of her own to stay alive.<br /><br />The saga that began with <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> takes its final turn as Shahrzad risks everything to find her way back to her one true love again.</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/46644989-lynn-gweeny"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/46644989-lynn-gweeny">Lynn Gweeny</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers‚Ä¶
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I thought this might be the reason: if you remember, Khalid's curse included the line, "I will take from you your dreams//I will take from you your ci<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">‚Ä¶more</a>
    I thought this might be the reason: if you remember, Khalid's curse included the line, "I will take from you your dreams//I will take from you your city." So the first time he avoided the executions, his city was taken from him by the drought. When he avoided Sharzad's execution, he couldn't sleep because HIS DREAMS WERE TAKEN FROM HIM. So, here, 'I will take from you your dreams' basically means 'I will rob you of your sleep'!<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_674').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1246066178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1246066178" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1246066178?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246066178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10171461216184584399"><blockquote>
  <i>No. He was not here to wreak revenge.<br/>For revenge was trifling and hollow.<br/>No. He was not here to retrieve his wife.<br/>For his wife was not a thing to be retrieved.<br/>No. He was not here to negotiate a truce.<br/>For a truce suggested he wished to compromise.<br/><br/>He was here to burn something to the ground.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>A very worthy sequel and conclusion to this magical, romantic story.</b><br/><br/>I said in my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_' title='The Wrath & the Dawn (The Wrath & the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wrath & the Dawn</a> that I'm just not much of a romantic person. I hate instalove, most love triangles, and genera</span>
  <span id="freeText10171461216184584399" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>No. He was not here to wreak revenge.<br />For revenge was trifling and hollow.<br />No. He was not here to retrieve his wife.<br />For his wife was not a thing to be retrieved.<br />No. He was not here to negotiate a truce.<br />For a truce suggested he wished to compromise.<br /><br />He was here to burn something to the ground.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>A very worthy sequel and conclusion to this magical, romantic story.</b><br /><br />I said in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> that I'm just not much of a romantic person. I hate instalove, most love triangles, and generally prefer romance to come behind more dangerous and exciting things. That being said, there is something about this world, its curses and its magic, that completely melts my heart.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308084.The_Rose___the_Dagger__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___2_" title="The Rose &amp; the Dagger (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #2) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose &amp; the Dagger</a> has the same <b>evocative, beautiful writing</b> as the first installment, but it is less about the romance. Don't worry, though, Shahrzad/Khalid shippers still have plenty to swoon over, but the relationship is more mature, less angsty, but no less emotional in this book. The time for flirtations is over - a curse must be broken and a kingdom must be saved.<br /><br />From magical books to flying carpets to giant serpents, this rich fantasy takes us on a rollercoaster ride. Many relationships and friendships are tested, challenged and broken apart as we discover more about Khalid's curse and the characters we think we know.<br /><br />There is <b>much betrayal and many surprises</b> (some real jaw-droppers!) over the course of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308084.The_Rose___the_Dagger__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___2_" title="The Rose &amp; the Dagger (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #2) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose &amp; the Dagger</a>. The writing flows with gorgeous description and the perfectly-told drama and action scenes propel the novel along at a fantastic pace.<br /><br />I particularly liked the introduction of Irsa - Shazi's younger sister. She is a very different kind of character. More nervous, not quite as comfortable in her own strength and ability, but this made it all the more satisfying when she was able to overcome her hesitations when it was required of her. It is infinitely more impressive to see a woman overcome her fears and decide to be strong, rather than simply being born that way.<br /><br />Perhaps most of all, <b>I love the final rise of "girl power" at the novel's climax</b>. <i>1,001 Nights</i> is a sexist story at its heart, and I was a little concerned about the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> simply turned it into a lusty romance. The novel ends on a high, powerful note for the strong, flawed, complex women of the novel. And I appreciated that touch a lot.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10171461216184584399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1363995339" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1363995339" />
    <a title="Sabaa Tahir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26226276-sabaa-tahir"><img alt="Sabaa Tahir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389816412p2/26226276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1363995339?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabaa Tahir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabaa Tahir" href="/user/show/26226276-sabaa-tahir">Sabaa Tahir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1363995339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5068864295524185930">This book is everything I wanted in a sequel. EVERYTHING. I don't know how Renee Ahdieh managed to make it even more amazing than the already amazing WRATH AND THE DAWN. Black magic, perhaps? Or maybe she's just insanely talented. Whatever the case, I adore this book. It's suspenseful, thoughtful, beautiful and sexy, a perfect follow-up to WRATH. <br/><br/> In fact, I think I'm going to go reread it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1638884597949412032"><i>‚ÄúCut the strings, Shazi. Fly.‚Äù</i><br/><br/>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br/><br/><b>The Rose & the Dagger</b> follows the aftermath of the burning in the city of Rey that occured only a week ago. Shahrzad and Khalid are separated from one another, yet longing to reunite.<br/>Going into this the only thing I was certain of was that I wanted a lot more of Khalid and a lot less of Tariq.<br/><br/>And it took some time to get to it, which I didn‚Äôt quite enjoy because Tariq continued to frustrate me in this</span>
  <span id="freeText1638884597949412032" style="display:none"><i>‚ÄúCut the strings, Shazi. Fly.‚Äù</i><br><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br><b>The Rose &amp; the Dagger</b> follows the aftermath of the burning in the city of Rey that occured only a week ago. Rey‚Äîand its ruler‚Äîare vulnerable. Shahrzad and Khalid are separated from one another, yet longing to reunite.<br>Going into this the only thing I was certain of was that I wanted a lot more of Khalid and a lot less of Tariq.<br><br>And it took some time to get to it, which I didn‚Äôt quite enjoy because Tariq continued to frustrate me in this book. He just made me feel extremely uncomfortable whenever he showed up:<br><br><i>‚ÄúShahrzad pushed away from him. ‚ÄúIt isn‚Äôt your place. I‚Äôve already spoken to Teymur. He won‚Äôt pursue the matter further.‚Äù<br>Tariq‚Äôs eyes flashed. ‚ÄúMy place?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúI‚Äôve handled the matter, Tariq. Do nothing, as it would serve no purpose, save to shed more blood. And I‚Äôve had enough of that.‚Äù She shouldered her way past him.<br>He cut her off, his jaw jutting forward, his fists at his sides. ‚ÄúWould you shackle the boy-king in such a manner?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúDon‚Äôt compare yourself to Khalid. It‚Äôs childish and beneath you.‚Äù</i><br>Yes exactly, thank you, Shazi.<br><br><i>‚ÄúYou will not seek revenge on my behalf, Tariq Imran al-Ziyad. I forbid‚Äî‚Äù<br>He grabbed her by the shoulders. ‚ÄúI will do as I damned well please, Shahrzad al-Khayzuran!‚Äù His voice was raw in its torment. ‚ÄúI denied myself what I wanted once out of principle, and not a day goes by that I don‚Äôt regret that decision with every fiber of my being!‚Äù</i><br>Every word and touch of his was nearly unbearable to read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461847924ra/18918757.gif" width="500" height="209" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean even he agreed towards the end that he was a fool.<br><i>‚ÄúTariq knew then‚Äîas he‚Äôd known when he‚Äôd read the letter Shahrzad kept tucked in her cloak‚Äîthat this was not an ordinary love born of a passing fancy.<br>In truth, Tariq had known even then that he could not win. That this was not a battle to be won.<br>Only a fool would have continued to think otherwise.<br>Yet Tariq had chosen to be a fool.‚Äù</i><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461847924ra/18918758.gif" width="240" height="309" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461848239ra/18918859.gif" width="240" height="309" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But thank the stars for Khalid because once it got to the good stuff, I was smiling and happy.<br><br><i>‚ÄúAre you truly not going to bring her back?‚Äù the Rajput asked.<br>‚ÄúWhat‚Äôs this?‚Äù Khalid finally grinned, though it was with a heavy heart. ‚ÄúAfter all your early protestations?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúDespite all, I find I . . . miss the little troublemaker. And how she made you smile.‚Äù<br>As did Khalid. More than he cared to admit to anyone.‚Äù</i><br>Right there with you, Khalid<br><br>But the story only started to pick up for me when Shazi met with Artan Temujin because it meant that she was getting one step closer to finding out about her magic and the curse bestowed on Khalid.<br><br><i>‚ÄúTrust is an interesting matter when it comes to Artan. He will not give it to those who do not offer it first.‚Äù</i><br><br>And my enthusiasm fully returned when Shazi told him the story of ‚ÄòThe Girl Who Grasped the Moon‚Äô‚Äîher storytelling skills are extremely captivating.<br><br><i>‚ÄúYou wanted to know why I agreed to help you. It‚Äôs mostly because Musa-abagha asked me to. And because I am bound by my ancestor‚Äôs foolishness. Bound to be a trapped granter of wishes. Musa-abagha has kept me safe these many years. Safe from those who would enslave me. Make of me a dragon who does nothing but bring gold necklaces to thankless little girls.‚Äù</i><br><br>Oh, and then one of my most anticipated moment in this book was finally happening:<br><br><i>‚ÄúAs her thumb brushed over the etchings carved into the jade, Shahrzad tried her best to ignore the undeniable weight settling around her heart.<br>The weight of realization.<br>And the thrill of certainty.<br>I‚Äôm going home.‚Äù</i><br>I was so thrilled and ecstatic. I had to calm my heart because my favorites were reuniting after all this time<br><br><i>‚ÄúHow much time had she wasted being afraid on the balcony?<br>Enough.<br>Squaring her shoulders, Shahrzad started for the screens‚Äî<br>And they slid open.<br>She halted in her tracks, refusing to look up.<br>Shahrzad knew it was Khalid. She sensed rather than saw him.<br>As always. As ever. As a rose to the sun.‚Äù</i><br>YES yes yes<br><br><i>‚ÄúHis eyes gleamed molten gold. And they said all without a word.<br>Shahrzad drew her sodden waves to one side, splashing water by his feet.<br>‚ÄúI‚Äôm sorry!‚Äù She wrinkled her nose. ‚ÄúThat was‚Äî‚Äù<br>He pulled her in to his chest, a hand tangling through her hair. The beat of his heart rang loud and true against her cheek. The only measure of time that mattered.<br>She exhaled fast only to inhale deep. To breathe in his scent. The scent of sandalwood and sunshine. Her fingers moved across his skin, making memories of their own. The hands of a master swordsman. The lips of her greatest love. The heart of a king.<br>‚ÄúKhalid.‚Äù</i><br>Damn, I could not have asked for a better reaction.<br><br><i>‚ÄúKhalid stared up at her, his features inscrutable‚Äî<br>His eyes inciting her heart to riot.<br>‚ÄúI‚Äôve missed the silence of you listening to me.‚Äù Shahrzad attempted a weak smile. ‚ÄúNo one listens to me as you do.‚Äù<br>His expression turned quizzical.<br>‚ÄúYou don‚Äôt wait to speak,‚Äù she clarified. ‚ÄúYou truly listen.‚Äù<br>‚ÄúOnly to you,‚Äù Khalid replied gently.‚Äù</i><br>His words were slowly killing me. Khalid and Shazi‚Äôs relationship is an unforgettable (and hot) romance.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461847924ra/18918759.gif" width="500" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But there weren‚Äôt enough moments between Shazi and Khalid to keep me satisfied. I feel like the major focus was on Tariq and the oncoming war. And I was really disappointed when Khalid got so close to killing off Tariq (twice) and then didn't.<br><br><i>‚ÄúIs she dead?‚Äù Tariq‚Äôs grief caused his voice to crack through the blue darkness. ‚ÄúJust answer that question, you bastard, and you may do as you please with me.‚Äù<br>‚ÄúWhy would I do anything for you?‚Äù the caliph replied, low and vicious.<br>‚ÄúBecause if she‚Äôs dead, I don‚Äôt care what happens to me!‚Äù<br>‚ÄúThen we agree on at least two things.‚Äù With that, the caliph shifted his attention toward Rahim, his swords glinting on a moonbeam.‚Äù</i><br><br><i>‚ÄúDo you worry about me, Khalid Ibn al-Rashid?‚Äù<br>The caliph hesitated, and that said more than words ever could. ‚ÄúThere was a time I did. But the fact that you waited until Shahrzad slept to touch her shows me you know she would not approve. You will not disrespect her in such a manner again. Nor will you disrespect me.‚Äù</i><br><u>Yes!</u> Finally someone called him out on it. The hate I have for Tariq is similar to how Khalid described his love for Shazi, <i>
  <b>‚Äúfrom the stars, to the stars.‚Äù</b>
</i> I‚Äôm seriously curious as to why Tariq wasn't killed off.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461847924ra/18918760.gif" width="273" height="273" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And just as I was thinking of writing down in my notes, ‚ÄúWhere‚Äôs Despina?‚Äù‚Äî she finally showed up: <br><i>‚ÄúEyes the color of a cerulean sky sparkled down at her.<br>Shahrzad‚Äôs chin struck her collarbone in horror.<br>‚ÄúHello, Brat Calipha.‚Äù<br>Despina.‚Äù</i><br><br><i>‚ÄúA crown.<br>The bitterness swelled within Shahrzad.<br>Despina had been many things to Shahrzad once. She‚Äôd been a friend when Shahrzad had most needed it. A confidante where Shahrzad had had none. But it was clear everything Shahrzad had known about Despina had been cloaked in lies. For it was beyond evident she was even more things now. The secret daughter of Salim Ali el-Sharif. A princess of Parthia. A spy and a deceiver.<br>Above all things, it was clear Despina had never been Shahrzad‚Äôs friend.‚Äù</i><br>I was truly shocked, and I didn‚Äôt get how she did a complete 180. Even in her short story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1587503669" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moth and the Flame</a> she sounded really genuine and not so bitter.<br><br><i>‚ÄúHow could you do this to Jalal?‚Äù Shahrzad asked, her nails digging into her palms as she tried in vain to suppress her seething outrage.<br>Her expression unnervingly apathetic, Despina spooned some pomegranate-and-pistachio rice onto her plate. ‚ÄúAlas, Jalal al-Khoury‚Äôs sentiments are no longer my concern.‚Äù Then she smirked at Shahrzad, and the feigned sympathy behind it made Shahrzad want to tear the band of shining stones from her crown of curls. ‚ÄúBut rest assured. The captain of the guard will have no trouble finding a willing girl to soothe his injured pride, of that I am certain.‚Äù The last words savored strangely of bitterness.‚Äù</i><br><br><i>‚ÄúHow does it feel, Shahrzad al-Khayzuran?‚Äù Despina said in a melodious voice. ‚ÄúTo be treated as a slave? To be the servant of people who see themselves as above you, when you know in your heart that you are the same?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúAsk your father,‚Äù Shahrzad retorted.<br>‚ÄúI‚Äôd rather ask your husband. When I next see him . . . kneeling at my feet.‚Äù</i><br>Without hesitation, Shahrzad splashed the remainder of her wine in Despina‚Äôs face.‚Äù<br>I <b>love</b> drama.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461847925ra/18918761.gif" width="200" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But then it turns out that she‚Äôs actually on Shazi‚Äôs side and I was so confused but also glad.<br><br><i>‚ÄúShahrzad resisted the urge to scream. ‚ÄúI‚Äôm not going anywhere with you, Despina el-Sharif. First you are one thing, then you are another. At this point, my neck hurts from spinning about so fast. Just tell me this: Why have you been lying to me this entire time?‚Äù</i><br><br><i>‚ÄúThen why did you come back at all?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúTo preserve our family.‚Äù Despina squeezed her hand. ‚ÄúNo matter the cost.‚Äù<br>Though a part of Shahrzad wanted to throw off Despina‚Äôs touch‚Äîto deny the touch of a girl tied in any way to Salim Ali el-Sharif‚ÄîShahrzad did not.<br>For it was the touch of a friend. Beneath it lay the strength of family.<br>‚ÄúYou deliberately provoked me at dinner, did you not?‚Äù Shahrzad asked quietly.<br>Despina tilted her head in rueful fashion. ‚ÄúWell, I did have to get you down into the palace prison somehow.‚Äù</i><br><br>And then I got to see her reunite with Jalal, which was magical.<br><br><i>‚ÄúA familiar, melodic laugh froze him in his tracks.<br>Without thought, Jalal began to run. He didn‚Äôt care if he left the fool in the dust behind him. At that moment, he didn‚Äôt care if he left all else in the dust behind him.<br>It wasn‚Äôt possible. His mind was playing tricks on him. As it was apt to do of late.<br>Jalal turned the corner. And skidded to a stop, nearly tumbling into the sand.<br>Just like that. She was there.<br>He saw no one else save her.<br>All else could go to the devil save her.<br>Despina.‚Äù</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461847925ra/18918762.gif" width="400" height="224" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But even though the last few chapters picked up the pace of the book, I felt a little underwhelmed with the majority of the story, especially when comparing it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1558854503" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a>‚Äî in TWTD we got incredible friendships, family, and love. And I feel that <i>The Rose &amp; the Dagger</i> lacked those important traits.<br><br>All in all, I feel as if the sequel wasn't as strong as its predecessor, the only parts that made me fall for the story (and not count the pages left in a chapter) were when Shazi and Khalid were together, which unfortunately wasn't enough.<br>The magic and the war were a background story in <i>The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</i> and I was really intrigued and willing to explore it in the sequel, yet it didn't compel me as much as the romance. Ren√©e Ahdieh definitely has a special talent for swoon-worthy romances, so I can't wait to read more of her writing in the future, but in this case the romance didn't really save the story for me. <br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>The Rose &amp; the Dagger</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0399171622/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0399171622&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=8f643be2d675b9fd46bf33f0b277a583" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482941798i/21564368.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482941798i/21564369.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

<div id="review_1106705554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106705554" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1106705554?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=awesome-romance">awesome-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=swoon-worthy-characters">swoon-worthy-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=holy-shit">holy-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=in-curand-in-romania">in-curand-in-romania</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106705554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14127608514400007494"><b>4.5 Stars</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <b>The rose‚Äôs rarest essence lives in the thorns.</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>The Rose and The Dagger</i> is an exquisite, superb, satisfying and clever finale. It will render you speechless with its intensity. Crush your heart a bit every few pages. Transform you into an addict of its gorgeous prose. But its true beauty lies in the fact that, somehow, you welcome it all with open arms. <br/><br/><a href='https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-H55FIp6g9xY/V2hD345ahEI/AAAAAAAAQIc/sA0WNzqqZF0vFAkOElj4R0uyoioeNXh2gCLcB/s1600/72d1c59682a46a0c1d409d4df6a10b24.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img height='320' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466451225i/19481195.jpg' width='218' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>If you don't get along with romance, shy away. Seriously, <i>shoo</i>. I'm just putting it like it is -- the romance and love story are</span>
  <span id="freeText14127608514400007494" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b> <br><br><i>
  <b>The rose‚Äôs rarest essence lives in the thorns.</b>
</i><br><br><i>The Rose and The Dagger</i> is an exquisite, superb, satisfying and clever finale. It will render you speechless with its intensity. Crush your heart a bit every few pages. Transform you into an addict of its gorgeous prose. But its true beauty lies in the fact that, somehow, you welcome it all with open arms. <br><br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-H55FIp6g9xY/V2hD345ahEI/AAAAAAAAQIc/sA0WNzqqZF0vFAkOElj4R0uyoioeNXh2gCLcB/s1600/72d1c59682a46a0c1d409d4df6a10b24.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466451225i/19481195.jpg" width="218" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If you don't get along with romance, shy away. Seriously, <i>shoo</i>. I'm just putting it like it is -- the romance and love story are what make these books great, the dominant ethos, the insanely good aspect. Sure, it has elements of magic, politics, self-discovery, but its core is represented by <b>the power of love</b>. And for a love-hungry sap like me, <b>THAT'S AWESOMENESS INCARNATE. </b><br><br><i>
  <b>‚ÄúIt was because they were two parts of a whole. He did not belong to her. And she did not belong to him. It was never about belonging to someone. It was about belonging together.‚Äù</b>
</i><br><br>There were two equally amazing things I absolutely loved. First, there's the fact that, thanks to the multiple POVs, it's not just Khalid and Shazi's dreamy love that has readers all hot and bothered and ethereally happy. Nope. Surprisingly, it's also Rahim and Irsa. And, of course, Jalal and Despina. All three relationships wonderfully developed, made with the intention of pulling on your heartstrings. <br><br>Secondly, there's a certain KICKASS aspect. <b>Women</b>. <i>
  <b>Empowering, badass, strong, young women.</b>
</i> The truth is that, in this universe, the women are put on a gold pedestal (rightfully so). They are revered, respected and treated as queens. There were so many instances were women had a role in the novels, starting with Khalid's mother's death that changed him forever, then the cruel curse unraveled because of a woman, 100 women doomed to die and a freaking war started because of a woman (insert Shazi here), the plot evolved thanks to these glorious characters and so they became the axis of the world and girls continued to omen the legacy in TRaTD. Marvelous Shazi, with her awe-inspiring backbone and infinite determination. Sweet Irsa, with her fair perspective on life and kind heart (who also reminded me so much of Prim from HG). Sneaky Despina, with her snark and cunning mind. And even Yasmine, who completed the set with a surprisingly emphatic behavior. <br><br>Coming back to the essential though -- Khalid and Shazi. These two are like magnets, soul mates, whatever you want to call them. There was a particular scene that ripped me to shreds where they were fighting to protect each other in the face of imminent and immediate danger. I think that visual captured the couple perfectly -- Khalid is not painted like a knight in shining armor, neither is Shazi painted like a damsel in distress. Far from it, actually. They are pictured as they should be -- a king and a queen that would rather die than see their loved one suffer. They are menacing, commanding and hella sexy, royalty coursing into every inch of their veins. <br><br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-QCYpXTYhUA8/V2hHcJ7-P7I/AAAAAAAAQIw/WMe0hZXLCvo-DExbz00ZO7pl6parKSqdwCLcB/s1600/6546cbca75e68e7524e2670b1f4fe3c2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466451991i/19481284.jpg" width="145" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>"Cut the strings, Shazi. Fly.‚Äù</b>
</i><br><br>Our spunky heroine did not change much, besides the short-lived interactions with her magical tendencies. She's still stubborn, feisty, arrogant and silver-tongued, but fierce, caring and astoundingly determined as well. What surprised me was her optimism, I didn't previously perceive her as the one to bring it forward, yet in comparison with the brooding, sulking caliph she was like a minion from Despicable Me. <br><br>Like the yang to the yin, Khalid completed Shazi in a regal manner. A strategist, an intelligent engineer and a terrifying swordsman, but this boy-king is still a boy and a romantic one at that. Holy intense, a goddamn poet that could turn us all enraptured girls into husks of die-hard fangirls and a devoted husband (that's putting it lightly). I've said back in my Wrath review, this man worships his wife and it was astounding to see how easily she can bring him to his knees. Yet he transforms. He starts to bear hope for a bright future with his love, in which they are together, with him healthy and 100% alive. And he starts fighting for it, making sacrifices and walking over his ego and colossal pride to ensure such happiness will be attained. <br><br><i>
  <b>‚ÄúNo. He was not here to wreak revenge.<br>For revenge was trifling and hollow.<br>No. He was not here to retrieve his wife.<br>For his wife was not a thing to be retrieved.<br>No. He was not here to negotiate a truce.<br>For a truce suggested he wished to compromise.<br><br>He was here to burn something to the ground.‚Äù </b>
</i><br><br>On top of that, he really did mature. For once, you could say he forgives. <b>His relationship with Tariq</b> (yeah, there is one) had me nearly in tears and their interactions were so consuming. I loved his sincere attempts of creating bonds with Irsa and his sadness and helplessness at the situation with Jalal was hard to see. Also, his turmoil about the fate of Khorasan was awful, with self-loathing and doubt shadowing his thoughts. But he slowly crumbled his walls and lets everyone witness the thoughtful and passionate young man lurking beneath his stoic facade. He became a true leader. <br><br><a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-tic2EJ_E87I/V2hH7PF5FFI/AAAAAAAAQI4/A40pPITCeWUGxaEgxOCUcZ4dW8itrztYwCLcB/s1600/0692566ea8f6d28e67b513a71083fc27.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466451991i/19481285.jpg" width="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>A wish of mine that turned true this installment was the deeper delving into the magic business. However, it was not as developed as I expected it to be. Regardless, I enjoyed the unique light upon Artan's legacy (a new and very interesting character) that added to the genius of the author's retelling. It was honestly brilliant. <br><br>Other characters have changed the plotline numerous times. Jahandar, for instance, was horrendous. I loathed the guy. Greedy and power-hungry and with no sense of a moral compass, he continued to toy with the lives of others like he did in the prequel. On the other hand, Tariq, who is usually an amazingly lovable boy, possessed a recklessness and impulsiveness that had me preparing for every ill-fated new development with an "Oh boy". <br><br>And so there were many such instances. I cried a bit at a particular scene in the end that had me internally screaming "IT'S NOT FAIR". My heart stopped soon after. And I picked up my jaw off the ground at some HOLY SHIT discoveries, the kind of twists that turn you stupid. Nonetheless, I smiled and laughed a lot. <br><br>Vikram needs to be mentioned: he was awesome. There was not nearly enough Jalal and Despina, but seeing Jalal so heartbroken and lovesick messed with my brains. And Jalal and Khalid's friendship had a rough phase which was sad to witness. To compensate, we got more of Tariq and Rahim's bromance which inserted a light-tone every here and there, although they are indeed a true force to be reckoned with if together.<br><br>The epilogue was so fitting and wonderful in all shades known to humankind. I mean -- that name eeeep!! I was so euphoric and grateful for this heartwarming closure. One thing's for sure -- this duology will remain one of my favorite series because it's no easy feat to trigger the whole emotional palette in me, yet these books succeeded in doing so -- I was happy, sad, angry, frustrated, bewildered, amused, in love. And thankful for the thrills, romance and adventures. <br><br><i>
  <b>"It‚Äôs late,‚Äù Khalid said. ‚ÄúYou should sleep.‚Äù <br>‚ÄúWhat are you talking about? I‚Äôm not doing anything.‚Äù <br>‚ÄúStop smiling and go to sleep.‚Äù <br>‚ÄúHow do you know I‚Äôm smiling? You‚Äôre not even looking at me.‚Äù <br>‚ÄúI can feel you smiling, Shazi.‚Äù</b>
</i><br><br>I wouldn't necessarily say this is better than Wrath (because honestly, in my view, it isn't), but I think I missed the mystery surrounding Khalid's killings the most. Since all was revealed, the slow burning intrigue and countless questions did not make an appearance in the sequel. However, that is not the reason I minimized the full rating by half a star -- the sole motive for that was that sometimes I simply felt my mind wandering off. Might have been my sleep deprived mind telling me to close the freaking book, might have been not. <br><br>Renee Ahdieh has established herself as a thorough, original and downright amazing author. There was big pressure on her shoulders due to the overwhelming and well deserved popularity of the first book, but she did not succumb to the nerves in order to give readers a meh book. No, she managed to take the world of Khorasan to greater heights. She managed to captivate her readers with developed characters, an engaging plot and swoons. Most importantly, she managed to prove that she's a kickass writer and the first book wasn't a fluke. Her style is different and compelling and I declare myself a definite fan. <br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-hMOEKJbsSZs/V2hIYRbgW3I/AAAAAAAAQJE/c6HLaB5Tie4V7Lp_zX7EroYxsrFrzFbWQCLcB/s1600/11140131.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="188" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466452099ra/19481312.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>The Rose and The Dagger</i> is an empowering, achingly beautiful sequel to one of the loveliest books ever. Soul-wrenching, yet uplifting all the same, this book has it all, from political vibes, Arabian spins on a famous story, doses of humor, gorgeous love stories interwoven with thrills of action, magic and a kaleidoscopic turn of events. It delivers the perfect kind of tale -- one side dished with great amount of heartbreak. Even so, you want more, and that's what makes it best. <br><br><i>
  <b>‚ÄúAs always. As ever. As a rose to the sun.‚Äù </b>
</i><br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3 <br></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14127608514400007494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1836198689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836198689" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836198689?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836198689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6306759009296726508">This review is about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308084.The_Rose___the_Dagger__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___2_' title='The Rose & the Dagger (The Wrath & the Dawn, #2) by Renee Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rose & the Dagger</a>, but I can't help but dedicate a few lines to the tragedy that hit Turkey last night. A couple of hours ago, my cheeks were stained with hot tears, because this book was <b>gut-wrenching</b>. But even more gut-wrenching were the minutes I spent later watching the news and shedding more tears, this time mourning the innocent victims and the fate of humankind. Humanity is a strange species, capable of hatred, and capable of love. It saddens me that we mostly emb</span>
  <span id="freeText6306759009296726508" style="display:none">This review is about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308084.The_Rose___the_Dagger__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___2_" title="The Rose &amp; the Dagger (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #2) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose &amp; the Dagger</a>, but I can't help but dedicate a few lines to the tragedy that hit Turkey last night. A couple of hours ago, my cheeks were stained with hot tears, because this book was <b>gut-wrenching</b>. But even more gut-wrenching were the minutes I spent later watching the news and shedding more tears, this time mourning the innocent victims and the fate of humankind. Humanity is a strange species, capable of hatred, and capable of love. It saddens me that we mostly embrace the former, and unleash mayhem and brutality instead of compassion and kindness. I want to believe that there is more in us. I <i>need</i> to believe it. And I pray for the people who perished because some of us chose savagery, and all those dark feelings that poison our souls. May they rest in peace.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúCut the strings, Shazi. Fly.‚Äù</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And she did fly. Shahrzad crossed deserts and visited Temples of Fire and fought fiercely, for her future and her loved ones were worthy of every sacrifice, every drop of blood and sweat, every threat and promise and suffering. This awful and wonderful girl would not cower against mercenaries and greedy sultans, she would never bow her head nor stop having faith in Khalid. Her beautiful monster. The monster that bled for his people, that trusted her judgement and valued her opinion and saw his equal in her. Their home was broken. Their enemy, ruthless. The war, inevitable. But Khalid and Shahrzad, the Caliph and Calipha of Khorasan, found the purest and most powerful magic of all. A magic worth dying for.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúIn the end, there is only time for love.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The conclusion of this <b>beguiling story</b> based on The Arabian Nights pierced my heart like a <b>dagger</b>, inflicting searing pain and tremendous agony. But it also healed my wounded heart, which blossomed like a <b>rose</b>, and filled me with hope, peace, and, most importantly, love.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481479447ra/21425747.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúThe power behind words lies with the person.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a> is a person of unlimited power, who weaves an intricate path towards your soul with her <b>eloquence</b> and the <b>sheer emotion</b> she pours into her words. There is something I can only describe as <b>gentlessness</b> in her writing, something that resembles a soft caress even when she is killing you. It is true that the first chapters were a little underwhelming, which was the effect of Khalid and Shahrzad's separation, but when their paths were aligned once more, everything fell back into place.<br>I was once more <b>ensnared</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481479447ra/21425748.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúIt was because they were two parts of a whole. He did not belong to her. And she did not belong to him. It was never about belonging to someone. It was about belonging together.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The relationship between Khalid and Shahrzad was <b>beautiful</b>. Their understanding and faith in each other were so touching they made my blood sing. They were lovers, friends, husband and wife, allies, <i>equals</i>. Khalid struggled to find his way back to light, but he never shied away from all the ugly things he did. He acknowledged them. And tried to atone for them. Shahrzad, stubborn and ill-tempered, never stopped fighting to make her wishes come true, to prevent a war and save everyone she held dear. Irsa, sweet and fragile Irsa, she was forged into a strong woman. Tariq and Rahim proved how honorable they were, despite the occassional lapses in judgement and blind hatred that led Tariq to fatal mistakes. Every character was flawed in his own way, but all of them were deeply <b>endearing</b>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúFrom the stars, to the stars.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>That's how much I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308084.The_Rose___the_Dagger__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___2_" title="The Rose &amp; the Dagger (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #2) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose &amp; the Dagger</a>.<br><b>From the stars, to the stars.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6306759009296726508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <i>magical</i>
</b> story. The Rose and the Dagger did not disappoint one bit. Although I felt that this book was not as great as the first, it was still every bit as <b>
  <u>majestic</u>
</b> as The Wrath and the Dawn.<br><br>The Rose and the Dagger is filled with many twists and turns, swooning (mostly over Khalid), and most of all... Heartbreak. This book will tug your heart in more ways than one. We will gain new friends and allies, same as we will lose our old ones. Some chapters were paced a bit slow, but I was <b>NOT</b> bored at all during any part of this book.<br><br>It was great to see our characters finally find peace with themselves and others. Shahrzad was as <b>
  <i>fierce</i>
</b> of a heroine as she always was in the first book. And if you thought Khalid was <b>swoon-worthy</b> in The Wrath and the Dawn, wait until you see him in The Rose and the Dagger.<br><br>I found that the ending felt a little rushed but it was still bittersweet nonetheless. I wish I could have more of this world and these characters because <b>
  <u>I'm in no way ready to let go of this wonderful world of love, magic, and storytelling</u>
</b> that Ren√©e has created for us.<br><br><b>
  <i>Thank you for this shining, shimmering, splendid magic carpet ride.</i>

<div id="review_2417453038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2417453038" />
    <a title="Reynita Maharani ‚òÖ The Night Reader ‚òÖ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader"><img alt="Reynita Maharani ‚òÖ The Night Reader ‚òÖ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579173421p2/43850323.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2417453038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18124249051693783452"><b> THE REVIEW IS POSTED </b><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i><br/>Love gave life to the lifeless. It was the greatest of all living <br/>powers.<br/></i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>I honestly don't know what to talk about because this book <b>
  <i>fucking ruined</i>
</b> me and left me without any words to utter from my mouth. I'm not complaining though. It's such a best feeling when books destroy me and hurt me emotionally and this book also lived up to my expectations. I swear I was so terrified when I started reading this book because I liked the first book but I nearly did not</span>
  <span id="freeText18124249051693783452" style="display:none"><b> THE REVIEW IS POSTED </b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i><br>Love gave life to the lifeless. It was the greatest of all living <br>powers.<br></i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>I honestly don't know what to talk about because this book <b>
  <i>fucking ruined</i>
</b> me and left me without any words to utter from my mouth. I'm not complaining though. It's such a best feeling when books destroy me and hurt me emotionally and this book also lived up to my expectations. I swear I was so terrified when I started reading this book because I liked the first book but I nearly did not finish the first book because it was so freaking boring at first, that's why I was terrified when I started reading this book. I was afraid that this book might bored me or I might did not finish it but thank God, none of that happened. I relished <b>
  <i>every single day I spent with this book.</i>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530967131ra/25937481.gif" width="330" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The Plot and the Pacing</u>
</b><br><br>The plot was so much better than the first book. It was so fucking awesome and such an action-packed book. <b>LIKE THAT WAS WHAT I HAD BEEN WAITING FOR AND I WAS NOT DISAPPOINTED AT ALL. </b>Ms. Ahdieh is a great author and I love her books and her writing style is so beautiful and amazing. Her books <b>always</b> manage to make me sob in happiness or pain. This book never bored me. Not even once. I always got shocked when I looked at the clock while I was reading it because time seemed flied so fast when I read this book. I did not even realize that I read the book for 4 hours straight! <br><br>For the pacing of the book, well it was rather slow at first but I already expected that would happen and even though, it was slow, it was not boring at all and some things also happened. So if you read this book and then you find it really slow at first, please don't stop reading it because the the book was slow at first but it was pretty fast-paced when the book was nearing the ending AND IT WAS SO WORTH IT AND I LOVE THIS BOOK AAAAAAAAA <br><br>and this book! I can't even. One moment I was laughing and the next moment I was sad and then after that I was angry and then after that I cried, I laughed and smiled. I LOVE THIS BOOK! NO I HATE THIS BOOK BUT I ALSO LOVE IT AAAAA <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530969801ra/25937677.gif" width="340" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>The Characters and the Romance</u>
</b><br><br>I loved all the characters in this book, well except some people though because they got on my nerves and they made me wish bad things upon them. So, in the first book I totally hated this certain character so much and I even wished for this person to just disappear and I did keep hating this person in this book but it did not last long and then after that all the hatred I felt toward this person vanished all at once. Yes, I did not agree with this person with so many things but then after that I sort of understood and I just felt like I wanted to give this person a warm hug and I just wanted to tell you again that this book made me cry ... a lot because of so many different reasons. I rarely cry these days but Ms. Ahdieh's books <b>always</b> make cry and just like I said that I loved all the characters in this book. Shahrzad was such a strong heroine and honestly, she was like my inspiration and Khalid, I have nothing to say about him except that I have this huge crush on him and I like him so much OH AND JALAL AND DESPINA, I LOVE THEM SOOOOOOO MUCH and the romance!! IT WAS SOOO SWEET. These characters brought so much happiness to me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530974422ra/25937962.gif" width="300" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But even though, I liked this book very much, there was still something that I did not like about it and it was the love triangle. I hate love triangle so much but the love triangle in this book was tolerable for me but I still did not like it at all. In my opinion, this book would be so much better without the love triangle. But again, the love triangle was not really bad, it was rather tolerable and the girl only loved one love interest. <br><br>I will surely miss all of these characters and I even felt sad when I finished reading this book because I enjoyed reading it and I still wanted to be with my friends and the people that I really liked but I was also happy when I finished it. Overall, it was such a great read for me and I enjoyed reading it immensely. <br><br>Thank you for reading and liking this review! I appreciate it so much guys and I hope you all have a fabulous day. Bye! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530972315ra/25937789.gif" width="340" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢<br><b>Tonight, I can sleep with happiness in my heart. REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW. </b><br>‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢<br><br><b>I literally hugged the book and squealed in delight when I got the book and if this book disappoints me, I'm sure I will just lay on the floor and cry üôÇüôÇ </b></span>

<div id="review_1409147631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409147631" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409147631?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409147631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4549016336455833843"><i> The Rose & the Dagger </i> was definitely a satisfying sequel to one of my favorite reads of 2015! It was so nice to be back in this beautiful world with some of my favorite characters. I do prefer <i> The Wrath & the Dawn </i> but I'm happy with the conclusion to this duology!<br/><br/>I chose to listen to the audiobook of this novel, which I think was a mistake on my part. This series can require extra attention when being read physically for me due to the flowing prose, so the detachment I sometimes get from lis</span>
  <span id="freeText4549016336455833843" style="display:none"><i> The Rose &amp; the Dagger </i> was definitely a satisfying sequel to one of my favorite reads of 2015! It was so nice to be back in this beautiful world with some of my favorite characters. I do prefer <i> The Wrath &amp; the Dawn </i> but I'm happy with the conclusion to this duology!<br /><br />I chose to listen to the audiobook of this novel, which I think was a mistake on my part. This series can require extra attention when being read physically for me due to the flowing prose, so the detachment I sometimes get from listening to an audiobook was not helpful. Especially considering it had been a year and a half since I had read the first book, it was EXTREMELY hard to jump into. I really did not retain the first few hours of the audiobook because of those factors. If you are an audiobook listener who multitasks and sometimes does not retain all the information, I may stray away from this one. That being said, I LOVED the audiobook! The narrator was fantastic and it was super enjoyable. It was also really nice to finally have correct pronunciation for all the (I believe it may be Persian?) names and locations. Despite the trouble I had getting into the story, I'm really glad I picked it up.<br /><br />Everything about <i> The Rose &amp; the Dagger </i> is what you could have wanted. It's the same flawlessly elegant writing, the superbly constructed characters and relationships, and the exciting storyline. I especially felt like there was more action/intense scenes in the sequel, which I particularly enjoyed. The only other slightly underwhelming part of this book was the ended; it felt very abrupt and unfinished. I felt there should have been another few chapters before the epilogue, or at least an expansion of the scenes leading up to the end.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this read and will continue to recommend &gt; The Wrath &amp; the Dawn <i> duology!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4549016336455833843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4533974288122281839">I wonder what a conversation with Ren√©e Adhieh would be like. <br/><br/>I could picture her in front of me, drinking tea perhaps, in a graceful manner and, of course, telling stories as though reliving them on the spot. As for me? I would be the listener, enraptured by her words, nodding my head every two seconds, my body still and my eyes fixed on her.<br/><br/>Except that would not be a conversation exactly, now would it? And I‚Äôm guessing my staring would be borderline creepy. Though there is no shame in being st</span>
  <span id="freeText4533974288122281839" style="display:none">I wonder what a conversation with Ren√©e Adhieh would be like. <br /><br />I could picture her in front of me, drinking tea perhaps, in a graceful manner and, of course, telling stories as though reliving them on the spot. As for me? I would be the listener, enraptured by her words, nodding my head every two seconds, my body still and my eyes fixed on her.<br /><br />Except that would not be a conversation exactly, now would it? And I‚Äôm guessing my staring would be borderline creepy. Though there is no shame in being star-struck‚Ä¶ especially when the star in question is a gifted storyteller. <br /><br />There is something about the way this author forms her sentences and expresses emotions in her stories that has me thinking magic is real. I know I sound cheesy right now and probably deserve a couple of eyes rolling at me. That‚Äôs fine, I can take it. Go ahead.<br /><br />But I so mean it. I can find a dozen things that are wrong with this sequel‚Äîplot holes, unconvincing politics, convenient outcomes, Tariq and Khalid‚Äôs new relationship, Shazi‚Äôs underwhelming and unused magical abilities‚Äîbut somehow Miss Ahdieh‚Äôs storytelling swept me off my feet in such a manner that all of these imperfections were dismissed from my mind by the part of me that wanted to consume more words signed Ren√©e Ahdieh. <br /><br />This goes back to my fictional conversation with the author presented above. I don‚Äôt know if you‚Äôve noticed‚Äîyou may have‚Äîbut this book is made of 70% of dialog. There is little action and adventure, perhaps because conversation is its essence. Proof? The characters manipulate and overthrow with their words, rarely with their swords. Even the few stories told are done so orally.<br /><br />Since I oh so enjoyed listening to what the characters had to say‚Äîand by extension the author herself‚ÄîI couldn‚Äôt have been happier reading this book. I made this realization only now as I‚Äôm writing this review. And now that I think about it, most books I end up disliking have little or tedious discourse between characters.<br /><br />Character and conversation-driven story. Loved it. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin‚Äô</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2243271391" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16055792883988427983">YAS QUEEN! everyone bow down to the calipha of khorasan! <br/><br/>ahhhhh. this was so amazing! while i saw <i>‚Äòthe wrath and the dawn‚Äô</i> as a clever love story intertwined with nuances of folklore legend and mystery, <i>‚Äòthe rose and the dagger‚Äô</i> is a daring tale of adventure and reckless abandonment. two perfect halves to one incredible story. and this second half elevated the story to a whole new level. so beautiful, so empowering, so heartbreaking, and so so unbelievable. <br/><br/>i am in awe at ahdiehs storytelling ab</span>
  <span id="freeText16055792883988427983" style="display:none">YAS QUEEN! everyone bow down to the calipha of khorasan! <br /><br />ahhhhh. this was so amazing! while i saw <i>‚Äòthe wrath and the dawn‚Äô</i> as a clever love story intertwined with nuances of folklore legend and mystery, <i>‚Äòthe rose and the dagger‚Äô</i> is a daring tale of adventure and reckless abandonment. two perfect halves to one incredible story. and this second half elevated the story to a whole new level. so beautiful, so empowering, so heartbreaking, and so so unbelievable. <br /><br />i am in awe at ahdiehs storytelling ability. she has mastered the art of duologies - by not stretching out a story past its limits, but also delivering enough so the reader doesnt feel cheated. this book (and series) delivered on all fronts. and it has definitely made me interested in looking into the tales of a thousand and one nights and experiencing the magic at its source.<br /><br />so sad, and yet so satisfied, this story is over. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>‚Ü† <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1277956641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277956641" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277956641?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277956641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15200116893521440980">4.5 stars. Trying to decide if I want to round up or down, so I'll round down for now. VERY worthy sequel/conclusion novel.<br/><br/><a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/05/swoon-thursday-173-rose-dagger-by-renee.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458228991i/18459663.png' width='250' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/05/review-rose-dagger-by-renee-ahdieh.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>The Rose & The Dagger by Renee Ahdieh<br/>Book Two of The Wrath & The Dawn series<br/>Publisher: G.P. Putnam's Sons Books for Young Readers<br/>Publication Date: April 26, 2016<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: Preordered copy<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>I am surrounded on all sides by a desert. A guest, in a prison of sand and sun. My family is here. And</span>
  <span id="freeText15200116893521440980" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Trying to decide if I want to round up or down, so I'll round down for now. VERY worthy sequel/conclusion novel.<br><br><a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/05/swoon-thursday-173-rose-dagger-by-renee.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458228991i/18459663.png" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/05/review-rose-dagger-by-renee-ahdieh.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br><br>The Rose &amp; The Dagger by Renee Ahdieh<br>Book Two of The Wrath &amp; The Dawn series<br>Publisher: G.P. Putnam's Sons Books for Young Readers<br>Publication Date: April 26, 2016<br>Rating: 4 stars<br>Source: Preordered copy<br><br>Summary (from Goodreads):<br><br>I am surrounded on all sides by a desert. A guest, in a prison of sand and sun. My family is here. And I do not know whom I can trust.<br><br>In a land on the brink of war, Shahrzad has been torn from the love of her husband Khalid, the Caliph of Khorasan. She once believed him a monster, but his secrets revealed a man tormented by guilt and a powerful curse‚Äîone that might keep them apart forever. Reunited with her family, who have taken refuge with enemies of Khalid, and Tariq, her childhood sweetheart, she should be happy. But Tariq now commands forces set on destroying Khalid's empire. Shahrzad is almost a prisoner caught between loyalties to people she loves. But she refuses to be a pawn and devises a plan.<br><br>While her father, Jahandar, continues to play with magical forces he doesn't yet understand, Shahrzad tries to uncover powers that may lie dormant within her. With the help of a tattered old carpet and a tempestuous but sage young man, Shahrzad will attempt to break the curse and reunite with her one true love.<br><br>What I Liked:<br><br>I already know that I have no idea how to review this book. It was utterly beautiful, just as breathtaking as one would expect. I knew I would love it, and I did. It's getting four stars from me, but my true rating is 4.5 stars. I am so in love with this duology! The story is definitely a favorite of mine. So don't mind too much if this review is short or vague or a bunch of fangirling!<br><br>At the end of The Wrath &amp; The Dawn, Shahrzad left Khorasan - and Khalid - and went to the desert, where her family had taken refuge. Her father was badly burned by a book of his (if you read book one, you know why). Irsa, Shahrzad's sister, has grown in Shahrzad's absence. And Tariq is distant, no longer the friend Shahrzad remembers. Shazi is determined to find a way to break Khalid's curse, and with the help of an ally, she may have found a way. Back at Khorasan. Khalid has been helping his city rebuild. He mourns the disappearance of his love, but a greater danger is looming. While Shazi is in the desert, learning her dormant powers and hunting for a way to help Khalid, Khalid is determined not to sacrifice any more girls, and to help his city recover. <br><br>One of the best things that Ahdieh did was reunite Shazi and Khalid *fairly* quickly. It was about 150 pages into the book, so you could look at that as quickly or not quickly. I thought it was pretty quick. A LOT happens in the first 150 pages though, mostly on Shazi's side.<br><br>Shazi is steadfast in her love for Khalid. Though she is in the desert and surrounded by her family that does not know the depth of her feelings for the "monster boy-king", she never wavers. She protects herself and defends herself and never stops trying to find a way back to Khalid. She isn't trapped in the desert (hello, flying carpet!), but she wants to return with good news for him.<br><br>We are introduced to some secondary characters that I adore. Irsa, Shazi's younger sister, is only fourteen (going on fifteen) but she is tough and strong and totally underestimated. Rahim is a soldier and Tariq's best friend. I like Rahim and Irsa's budding romance. I don't like Tariq and never will. Same with Shazi's father. We don't see too much of Jalal, or Despina, or the Rajput, but we learn more about them on personal levels, and they all play a huge role in the book. I didn't love Jalal like I did in book one, but he has good reason for being the jerk he was in this book.<br><br>Khalid. Khalid deserves his own paragraph. I love this man of few words, with few expressions and few weaknesses. He is misjudged though not underestimated, and he carries a heavy burden that most do not know of or understand. I love his fierce protectiveness over Shazi, and how he lets her be and doesn't try to control her. I love how he loves her. I love how she loves him.<br><br>I love the romance. Looking back, I don't even know how I was worried about a love triangle. Tariq had no chance with Khalid in existence. Even with Khalid not in existence... Shazi loved Tariq as a friend. I felt a little bad for Tariq, but also I didn't, because he is a huge idiot and deserves terrible things that never came his way. There were many unforgivable things he did, especially in this book. Anyway, I loved the romance between Khalid and Shazi. I love how it blossoms, how they lean on each other and trust each other. I love how their relationship never wavers, only strengthens.<br><br>The big-picture issue in the series goes beyond Khalid's curse - there are masses that want to destroy Khalid's empire. I like how the author intersects these two important points of the story - Khalid's curse, and the impending war.<br><br>So, characters were amazing. Khalid was my favorite, Shahrzad in close second. The character development was well-written. The writing was absolutely beautiful. The romance was wonderful. This conclusion novel was all kinds of stunning!<br><br>The ending is a rollercoaster! But so, so satisfying (except for one thing, which I will mention next). I am in love with this story! I adore how the author ends the series - it seemed pretty wonderful to me. And you know how much I love a good HEA!<br><br>What I Did Not Like:<br><br>Khalid and Jalal have a sort of, um, disagreement, in this book. And Jalal says some pretty harsh things and turns his back on Khalid. Given the epilogue, from what I can indirectly infer, this fight is very much in the past, by the end of the book. But I wish the author would have shown the reconciliation between the two cousins, explicitly. In fact, Jalal all but disappears from the story, after this argument. I wanted to see the men patch things up, do the bromance thing. This is my one complaint about this book - their relationship needed to be addressed, at the end of the book, when all was said and done.<br><br>Would I Recommend It:<br><br>I highly highly HIGHLY recommend this book. And the first book. Haven't read The Wrath &amp; The Dawn? Fix that. There is no reason not to, now that the series is complete! Plus there are a few short stories on Amazon that are free (and one Jalal/Despina novella that is $1.99) to enjoy as well - not that you *need* to read any of those. This series, overall, is easily a favorite. I don't throw around the word "favorite" often!<br><br>Rating:<br><br>4.5 stars -&gt; rounded down to 4 stars. While this book isn't one of my rarely dubbed favorites, this series in general definitely is. Thank you, Renee Ahdieh, for blessing the world with your beautifully written story of Khalid and Shahrzad.<br><br><br><br><strong>My WRATH collection!</strong><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463781122i/19158972._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Pre-publication squees:</strong><br><br>NEEEEEDDDD!!!!!!!!!!!<br><br>Kinda hoping this series is just a duology and nothing longer... less painful waiting and whatnot ;)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410457450ra/11110018.gif" width="390" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>EDIT: 10/02/2015 -- COVER COVER COVER WE HAVE A COVER!!!! It is amazing! THANK YOU, Penguin, for sticking with that same design. <a href="http://www.bustle.com/articles/114407-renee-ahdiehs-the-wrath-and-the-dawn-sequel-the-rose-and-the-dagger-spins-more-beautiful" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out the official cover reveal on Bustle</a>!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15200116893521440980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
