<div id="review_1626792970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626792970" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1626792970?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780399546631" href="/book/show/28248583-the-rose-and-the-dagger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626792970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12330854395314134899"><b>‚ÄúI‚Äôve missed the silence of you listening to me.‚Äù Shahrzad attempted a weak smile. ‚ÄúNo one listens to me as you do." His expression turned quizzical. ‚ÄúYou don‚Äôt wait to speak,‚Äù she clarified. ‚ÄúYou truly listen.‚Äù</b><br/><br/>To make matters clear: <b>if you loved or, anyway, truly enjoyed <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i>, then you'll love this too</b>. It is everything a devoted fan could ask of a series conclusion.<br/><b>My problem</b> was -is- that <b>Shahrzad and Khalid's relationship</b> never spoke to me; actually, I think my appreciation</span>
  <span id="freeText12330854395314134899" style="display:none"><b>‚ÄúI‚Äôve missed the silence of you listening to me.‚Äù Shahrzad attempted a weak smile. ‚ÄúNo one listens to me as you do." His expression turned quizzical. ‚ÄúYou don‚Äôt wait to speak,‚Äù she clarified. ‚ÄúYou truly listen.‚Äù</b><br /><br />To make matters clear: <b>if you loved or, anyway, truly enjoyed <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i>, then you'll love this too</b>. It is everything a devoted fan could ask of a series conclusion.<br /><b>My problem</b> was -is- that <b>Shahrzad and Khalid's relationship</b> never spoke to me; actually, I think my appreciation of the above-mentioned couple is fundamentally <b>undermined </b>by 1) the insta-love (don't try to deny it; seriously, don't) and 2) the fact that, in <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i>, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[their first intercourse, if you think of it, happens under the banner of "I'm your husband, we're supposed to do this, we will do this" and, as if that were not enough, when it is openly specified that Khalid never touched his wives before they were sent to die. Why did he have to impose himself on her and her only, then? I'm sorry, I can't ship a couple that involves this person. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />‚Ä¢So, first issue: <b>I never felt the slightest involvement in this ship</b>, because of the reasons above. I knew what I was getting into, I didn't rely on that to begin with, It didn't particularly influenced my rating because I had taken that into account from the start.<br /><br />‚Ä¢I'm still <b>not a fan of Shahrzad</b>. In Italy, we have a saying that more or less goes, "you can't even dare tell her how beautiful her eyes are," meaning that she's one of those people that, if you so much as raise a hand to greet them, they are likely to spit in your face and possibly throw a dagger at you for no reason at all. That's not called being badass, that's called being <b>hysterical</b>.<br /><br />‚Ä¢<b>New characters whose utility is rather debatable</b> (why, this very much seems to be an issue with all the books I've read of late). You understand that their utility <i>really</i> was debatable when, at the end of the story, you realize all they had to do was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[die and create a little more <b>drama</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. How deliciously professional. A pity that someone forgot to actually work on the part "make the reader care".<br /><br />‚Ä¢<b>The curse</b>- I mean, it wasn't completely <i>bad</i>, at least it had some logic, but: that's it? A whole book focused on this thing, and then the plot gets rid of it and <b>veers</b> like this, as if this curse had had no importance to begin with? It was so <b>brusque</b> and <b>ungraceful</b> I'm still suffering from whiplash after-effects.<br /><br />‚Ä¢I remembered liking the <b>writing</b> in <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i>, but I certainly despised it here. <b>Declamatory</b>, <b>pompous</b>, <b>histrionic</b>, <b>high-sounding</b> and fastidiously so. I lost count of how many sentences began with "For" instead of "Because", but I'm sure once I found at least five in less than two pages. Alas! (Yes, another abundant presence. Ugh.)<br /><br />‚Ä¢<b>Tariq</b> was <b>annoying</b>. And I'm not going to say another word on the matter, because, all the tropes related to a love-triangle you can think about? They're here.<br /><br />‚Ä¢<b>Da Powah To Luuurve</b>. Please. Do I look like a five-year old to you?<br /><br />‚Ä¢I thought I needed to control my blood glucose after that <b>epilogue</b>. I may have also faked a gag. Sorry, but that level of gushiness was beyond human comprehension.<br /><br />‚ûΩ Basically, the main perk of this book is that it <b>puts an end to this series rather nicely</b>, and, even though I didn't care for these characters and wasn't particularly captivated by the plot, it didn't bore me. I did have a good time and was able to enjoy some hours of sweet doing nothing, with my brain temporarily shut. And that was just what I wanted: nothing more, nothing less.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12330854395314134899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1630223007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630223007" />
    <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey"><img alt="Mohammed Arabey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364338486p2/13592557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630223007?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohammed Arabey" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey">Mohammed Arabey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630223007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12108699871144514931">Arabian Nights are fast thrilling epic stories mixing with a passionate love story, that really takes you a whole new world...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468429743ra/19705563.gif' width='450' height='269' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>And this different retelling still one of the kind that worth your time..complete with Love, curse, Black Magic...<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468628382i/19729989._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='257' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>BUT it didn't live up to the epic that start building up in book one and its grand ending..<br/>For a duology it could've been faster, more focused. yet book two's missing sparks..less magical stories..less fiery love.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468432709i/19706058._SX540_.png' width='450' height='330' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The biggest reason of enjoying this book was th</span>
  <span id="freeText12108699871144514931" style="display:none">Arabian Nights are fast thrilling epic stories mixing with a passionate love story, that really takes you a whole new world...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468429743ra/19705563.gif" width="450" height="269" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And this different retelling still one of the kind that worth your time..complete with Love, curse, Black Magic...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468628382i/19729989._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="257" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>BUT it didn't live up to the epic that start building up in book one and its grand ending..<br>For a duology it could've been faster, more focused. yet book two's missing sparks..less magical stories..less fiery love.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468432709i/19706058._SX540_.png" width="450" height="330" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The biggest reason of enjoying this book was that I loved the characters and the atmosphere of book one much that I was glad to revisit one more time, To see how can the epic started by the end of book one would ends. Some characters got good conclusion for their stories...some just got weaker or shallow or went totally missing.<br>So, if I rated book one 3.5 : 4, the sequel is just 3 : 3.5..<br><br>But let's start with the..<b>
  <u>
    <blockquote>The Story</blockquote>
  </u>
</b><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462495145i/19004942._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Though it picks up right after the epic finale of book one‚Ä¶ the first half of the book lacks thriller or any new "important" events.<br>Some good drama scenes was here but lost in many filler ones.<br>The story mainly about Shahrazad searching for a way to stop the curse on her Beloved Khaled..and the spell of the dark book with her father.. using the Magic Carpet she reach the fire template to have some answers..<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really hate how they easily solved the 2 unrelated curses with one simple solution.. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468595626i/19726614._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="231" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also the Bedouin idling the attack to overthrow the Caliph. Two third of the book till any plan took action.<br>Even Shazy stories -just two actually- was good but I didn't get the point of it. Didn't have the effect to the story as in book one.<br><br>There's a good setting for an epic conflict, I must admit that I hate reading prolonged war sequence, but also I don't enjoy disappointing waste of a chance to bring an epic one.<br>Yes , good talk can solve everything...but not always makes a good story..<b>
  <u>
    <blockquote>The Love <s>Story</s> Stories</blockquote>
  </u>
</b><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468598363i/19727121._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="281" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Stronger &amp; as very convenient as book one.<br>It's more and took larger part, and though I am not love stories fan but still Renee Ahdieh convinced me to fall in love with her beloved character and convenient way to draw her story beautifully and make it living.<br><b>
  <blockquote>‚ÄúKhalid/Shahrazad/Tariq‚Äù<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468598520i/19727132._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote>
</b>We finally reach the very well written conclusion to the Love triangle.<br>I really enjoyed it, it may look impossible to have a peaceful ending but the author really good in making it smoothly.<br><br>I didn't like a scene at the beginning between Tariq and Shazy since I am so in love with the love between Shazy and Khaled... and in this part it's really in its best..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468599357i/19727257._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="172" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But I really hated the chapter before the last, the supposed death, it was really a waste of drama. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>
  <blockquote>‚ÄúDespina and Jalal‚Äù<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468622922i/19729644.jpg" width="290" height="375" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote>
</b><br>I adore Despina, there's good story here full of surprises and twists. I may be not 100% convenience by a certain twist but still I love reading it.<br>By the way the only ‚Äúworthy‚Äù prequel to read for me was ‚ÄúThe Moth &amp; The Flame‚Äù that revolves around them. And adding depth into the 2 beloved characters.<br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692718250" rel="nofollow noopener">The Review</a><br><b>
  <blockquote>‚ÄúIrsa &amp; Rahim‚Äù<blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote>
</b><br>It was a filler for me.. it serves little to the story anyway but I like Irsa character so much specially her relation with her sister.<br>But clearly it's just a filler served to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[present a sacrifice.. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>
  <u>
    <blockquote>The Rest of the Characters</blockquote>
  </u>
</b><br><b>‚ÄúArtan‚Äù</b><br>I was interested to see more of this mystical world and his family, alas it only served as quick solving to ends two curses in one strike.. I kinda felt cheated.<br>He really could been used better and more magical and serve more epic scenes.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468626630i/19729874._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="281" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>‚ÄúSheikh Omar‚Äù</b><br>Though his role wasn't big I liked his obsession with good love stories. The author make sure I feel like him with her beautifully illustrated Khaled and Shazy love.<br><br><b>‚ÄúJahandar‚Äù</b><br>God, is he really that stupid? Till the end? <br>The father of Shazy really gets more stupid each new chapter...May be the attempt he made by the end and how it solved effects more in my decision to rate.<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>And this book got more parts from other characters‚Äô perspective than in book one.<br>Yet there were more characters thatcould have been better if they used well than this. <br><b>
  <u>
    <blockquote>Finally</blockquote>
  </u>
</b><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462494527i/19004886._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="336" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The writing style is easy and enjoyable.<br>Enjoyable but can easily be boring sometimes.<br>Sometimes when there's lots of repeats.<br>Repats just what I do here.<br>Here in this paragraph.<br>Paragraph.<br><i>Got it?</i><br>Anyway,<br>It's really still one of the best YA deals with romance in a good way, food in a very delicious way -it really makes my mouth watering..-not many feasts like book one but still delicious enough-<br>It has some awesome dramatic scenes..<br><br>I loved the use of some arabian words -But still Calipha is for man not woman- and I didn't know Nabulsi is a famous soap.<br><br>I may be a bit disappointed because I needed more, and sure the plot could have handled more magical epics..more fairy stories..The epic was reduced to pass a message that good talk can solve anything... <br> Yet I will wait to read more by Renee. who made me fly a good length into one really good love story... Arabian Nights story<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468628157i/19729960.jpg" width="450" height="245" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And will search for more Arabian Nights retelling.<br><br>Mohammmed Arabey<br>From 6 July 2016<br>To 10 July 2016<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Next stop; A Thousand Nights.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462495672i/19004978._SX540_.jpg" width="375" height="281" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>
</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText1328913990309732274" style="display:none"><br />No, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308084.The_Rose___the_Dagger__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___2_" title="The Rose &amp; the Dagger (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #2) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose and the Dagger</a> is far from being perfect but the prose is such a brilliant, beautiful narrative making this series an unforgettable, thrilling, adventurous, fantasy- romance. I savored every remarkable moment, every dazzling word and every stirring emotion in the story. It makes me want to sing Disney songs and twirl. It‚Äôs true, this series can be considered sappy, cheesy and even melodramatic but it‚Äôs just so beautifully written that it seems to have this disabling effect on me making my knees wobbly, my eyes sparkling in complete awe leaving me into an un-salvageable, swooning puddle. <br /><br />The plot started off right where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath and the Dawn</a> ended and it brought back all the wonderful memories instantly transporting me to this magical world. It didn‚Äôt take long for me to be once again trapped in a flurry of emotions for these characters that captivated me from the very start. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Poor Rahim, though. I wish he didn‚Äôt have to die. Poor Irsa. *sniffs* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br /> I do not usually approve of love triangles but in this story, it‚Äôs not only beautiful but it also seems necessary as it is the plot‚Äôs very core uniting the two heroes in their mission because of their love for the same, strong-spirited woman who is not only beautiful (I admit I was a bit annoyed at the countless times her beauty was mentioned) but brilliant, smart, snarky and selfless as well. I admire Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a>‚Äôs wise decision to do away with war and bloodbath usually found in fantasies‚Äô finale and instead resorted to witty plot twists involving smart and beautiful women. Applause! <br /><br />It‚Äôs true some wars can be won before they even get started just like this series winning my heart over without a fight.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1280805934?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joelle (Throne of books) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joelle (Throne of books) " href="/user/show/17660097-joelle-throne-of-books">Joelle (Throne of books) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1280805934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer513823283128316128">Another one bites the dust. <br/>To say I'm disappointed, is a huge understatement. Last year, THE WRATH & THE DAWN was one of my favorite reads of the year. This year however, with this sequel, it is being added to my disappointing sequels list. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, I did enjoy it. But I did not love it. Once again Ren√©e's writing is absolutely mesmerizing. But the story? Slow and a little boring. It wasn't until about the last 130 pages that the pace picked up and I started enjoying it a bit more. <br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText513823283128316128" style="display:none">Another one bites the dust. <br />To say I'm disappointed, is a huge understatement. Last year, THE WRATH &amp; THE DAWN was one of my favorite reads of the year. This year however, with this sequel, it is being added to my disappointing sequels list. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I did enjoy it. But I did not love it. Once again Ren√©e's writing is absolutely mesmerizing. But the story? Slow and a little boring. It wasn't until about the last 130 pages that the pace picked up and I started enjoying it a bit more. <br /><br />I loved Shazi and Khalid, serious heart eyes. Shazi's sass and quick mouth is so me to be frankly honest. I LOVED the relationship between her sister and Rahim. And there were the characters I still don't like. Tariq, ever the annoying love sick puppy who makes stupid stupid decisions and is even more stubborn than a frog who refuses to move from where he's sitting. Shazi's father (also very effing stubborn.), basically every other character. <br /><br />As a conclusion to a duology, I did not like it. Everything was resolved too simply and easily, too conveniently. The revelations and plot twists did surprise me and the ending was heart eyes and heart throbs and rainbow stained tears but overall I simply wish this hadn't been a duology, I wish more events had gotten in the way of the characters, and for that, I personally like to have that all build up between a book or two. Duologies just make everything feel very rushed and lacking in certain areas.</span>

<div id="review_1406867351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1406867351" />
    <a title="Sarah DiMento" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7883731-sarah-dimento"><img alt="Sarah DiMento" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491621798p2/7883731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1406867351?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah DiMento" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah DiMento" href="/user/show/7883731-sarah-dimento">Sarah DiMento</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1406867351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17330455066174508040"><b>
  <i>"Where is your heart, Sharzad al-Khayzuran?" His voice was course in its insistence.<br/>In an alley by the souk. In a night of oblivion.<br/>In the promise of tomorrow." </i>
</b><br/><br/>Initial reaction: Well, I finally finished this after weeks of reading slump. I'm giving this a generous four stars because I had some problems with it, but really really wanted to love it the way I loved the first book. Renee Ahdieh is an amazing romance writer, but a not so amazing fantasy writer, in my opinion. Nevertheless, this </span>
  <span id="freeText17330455066174508040" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Where is your heart, Sharzad al-Khayzuran?" His voice was course in its insistence.<br />In an alley by the souk. In a night of oblivion.<br />In the promise of tomorrow." </i>
</b><br /><br />Initial reaction: Well, I finally finished this after weeks of reading slump. I'm giving this a generous four stars because I had some problems with it, but really really wanted to love it the way I loved the first book. Renee Ahdieh is an amazing romance writer, but a not so amazing fantasy writer, in my opinion. Nevertheless, this book was beautifully written and overall a satisfactory end to the story. Full review to come!<br /><br />===============================================================<br /><b>
  <i>"Love was something that did much to change a person. It brought joy as it brought suffering, and in turn brought about those moments that defined one's character.<br />Love gave life to the lifeless. It was the greatest of all living powers." </i>
</b><br /><br />I wrote my review in list format, it seemed the best way to convey my thoughts:<br /><br /><b>Things I Loved About The First Book:</b><br />1. The romance- Shazi and Khalid OTP OTP OTP!!<br />2. The subtle and mysterious nature of magic (granted, magic did not play a major role in the first book)<br />3. The beautiful writing<br />4. The descriptions of food (yea, I said it. I was perpetually hungry throughout the first book.)<br />5. The characters and their development<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Why don't you start by saying aloud what it is you wish for?"<br />Could she even dare say such a thing? After all the death and bloodshed and senseless destruction, it seemed like the worst kind of selfishness.<br />To build her world upon a bower of bones.<br />"So tiresome." Shiva nudged her in jest. "This is your dream, you goose! If you cannot say what it is you desire in your own dream, then where can you dare to say it?" </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>What I Expected From The Second Book:</b><br />1. More Shazi and Khalid. Maybe more Despina and Jalal?<br />2. An explanation and exploration of the way magic works. <br />3. An exciting and action packed story in which our protagonists utilize magic to break this curse!<br />4. More beautiful writing<br />5. More descriptions of food<br />6. More characters and their development<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Your future is not set in stone, my dearest star. A coin turns on itself a number of times before it lands."</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>What I Got From The Second Book:</b><br />1. Not so much Shazi and Khalid, and certainly not Despina and Jalal. This would not necessarily be a bad thing, I don't need romance to enjoy a book, BUT:<br />2. No world-building, no explanation of magic, messy and pointless elements of plot, everything resolved waaaaaaay too easily <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ like okay, we have to destroy this book to break the curse. Then when it comes time to destroy the book, Khalid just stabs it and collapses from exhaustion and that's it: Book destroyed, curse ended. Way too easy. When does anything ever happen like it supposed to?! Or how Shazi just realizes at the end that her magic stems from what she touches, like how did she just realize this?! And I still don't really get it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And why doesn't Khalid know more about magic? I mean.. he's the king.. you think he'd want to know. To do some research on curses and how to break them? Especially considering how easily resolved this whole thing was. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ When Shazi shows up on her carpet he's all disbelieving and shocked, but I feel like a king should know this kind of thing is possible!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Honestly, this book made me question Khalid a little. How could you accept your curse so easily? Did you even try to find a way out?! Whew.. Ok /end rant<br />3. Beautiful writing. The writing alone will compel me to read anything Renee Ahdieh writes.<br />4. Very little description of food... Waaaaaah :(<br />5. Introduction of a couple interesting characters... Namely, Irsa and Artan. I wish Artan's character had been explored more. That whole part of the story left a lot of questions for me and was a missed opportunity for world-building and explaining the magic system, in my opinion.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"This makes the second- no, wait- third night in a row you've arrived at the temple and ruined my evening with the moon."<br />She unfurled to her feet, dusting off her palms. "Pardon me for ruining what would have been an otherwise productive evening." </i>
</b><br /><br />Was this a bad book? No no no no. I love these characters, I love Renee Ahdieh's writing, and I was happy with the way the story ended. I was just a little let down and expected a bit mooooore. I loved the overall theme of the book: becoming the person you want to be (Khalid becoming the king he wants to be, Irsa becoming braver and less like a mouse [as she would say]) and creating your own destiny. Shazi was a bit arrogant to me at times, but I've always appreciated her bold and strong nature. Overall, this duology belongs in my favorites and I would recommend to anyone who enjoys YA romance, fantasy, historical fiction. You won't regret it :)<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"But, if you ask me, the best way to go about flying is to cut the strings tying you down... Cut the strings, Shazi. Fly." </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17330455066174508040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1487562838" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544410363p2/14772037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1487562838?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=4-star-books">4-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=fall-2016-tbr">fall-2016-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1487562838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8728762535760269501"><b>‚ÄúGive me a meaningful love or a beautiful death!‚Äù</b><br/>Simply exquisite. A book of <b>dreams</b>,<br/> <i>struggles</i><br/> <b>wishes</b><br/> <i>corruption</i><br/> <b>fullfillment</b><br/> <i>heartache</i><br/> <b>love</b><br/> <i>sacrafice</i><br/> <b>magic</b> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479141463ra/21153006.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><p> This book utterly takes my breath away. The writing is beautiful and the story has depth. Characters are developped, there is sadness and despair, there is tragedy. There is also love, magic and hope. This is a tale as old as time that will always be timeless. </p><p>
  <br/>
  <b>‚ÄúIt was because they were two parts of a whole. He did not belong to her. A</b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText8728762535760269501" style="display:none"><b>‚ÄúGive me a meaningful love or a beautiful death!‚Äù</b><br>Simply exquisite. A book of <b>dreams</b>,<br> <i>struggles</i><br> <b>wishes</b><br> <i>corruption</i><br> <b>fullfillment</b><br> <i>heartache</i><br> <b>love</b><br> <i>sacrafice</i><br> <b>magic</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479141463ra/21153006.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p> This book utterly takes my breath away. The writing is beautiful and the story has depth. Characters are developped, there is sadness and despair, there is tragedy. There is also love, magic and hope. This is a tale as old as time that will always be timeless. </p><p>
  <br>
  <b>‚ÄúIt was because they were two parts of a whole. He did not belong to her. And she did not belong to him. It was never about belonging to someone. It was about belonging together.‚Äù </b>
  <br>
</p><p> I praise Renee Ahdieh for this duology and her attention to details. The story almost feels as though it comes alive with magic. I can't wait for more books written by her! I highly encourage anyone who has not read the wrath and the dawn (the first book) to pick it up. If you are like me and read the wrath and the dawn but neglected to pick up the rose &amp; the dagger for a long time, stop neglecting it. I don't know why I put it off for so long, it was a fantastic read.</p><p>
  <br>
  <br>
  <b> The rest of my review will contain spoilers as I discuss the events/plot of the book! <b><br>WOWZA. What a finish. <br></b></b>
</p><p>I honestly did not know this series was a duology until I started reading it. I wondered how this book would wrap everything up. It rose to the challenge.</p><br><b>‚ÄúFor nothing, not the sun, not the rain, not even the brightest star in the darkest sky, could begin to compare to the wonder of you. Khalid‚Äù <b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469449231ra/19818543.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></b></b><p>I was really happy to see Isra meet somebody, but then felt so much sympathy for when Rahim died. Speaking of Rahim‚Äôs death..it was totally Tariq‚Äôs fault. As readers know, Khalid was not going to attack, he held himself back because he knew what would happen. Tariq did not have that control. Provoked and angry he attacked, not able to evaluate the consequences. If he hadn‚Äôt Rahim would most likely still be alive. YET KHALID TOOK THE BLAME. Yes Tariq said it was his own fault but Khalid disagreed, explained it was only his fault and took the guilt. Ughhhhhh Tariq was so frustrating during this book. Most of the time he was not frustrating and absolutely his actions were understandable. BUT when he began the attack on Salim, also when he shot Shazi (aiming for Khalid) was extremely irritating. By the end of the book he had learned and sided with Khalid *finally* </p><p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479141463ra/21153007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>‚Äúif you ask me, the best way to go about flying is to cut the strings tying you down ‚Äù </b><br>I really enjoyed Artan and Omar as characters. I thought they were good additions to the book.<br>Jahandar pissed me off.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403158189ra/10050732.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Jahandar has literally ruined everything. He launched a storm killing innocent lives and destroying a city. He kidnapped his daughter against her will for something he thought was best. HE ASSINATES (sort of) THE LOVE OF HIS DAUGHTERS LIFE.<br>That second last chapter had me DYING. I knew Jahandar was killing himself in the end of that chapter but I didn‚Äôt know that he did that while saving Khalid. So when the next chapter or ‚Äòepilogue‚Äô came around, I thought this was someone‚Äôs dream. Until they mentioned his scar, then I was like OHHHHH I SEE WHAT HE DID.<br>I thought the last chapter/epilogue was really cute and pleased me to see how the characters were living. ALSO YASMINE AND TARIQ! I SHIP IT!<br>I also loved when Yasmine, Despina and Shazi worked together because that was one of things I wanted to see comign out of the first book. I think they'd work well as friends. That made me really excited.<br>Despina took me on a rollar coaster ride. First I was like ohh she‚Äôs running away from Jalal because she doesn‚Äôt think he loves her or will marry her. So she thought she‚Äôd marry the Rajput instead. I was sympathetic. THEN AT THAT DINNER PARTY I WAS FUMMING LIKE OH NO, NO YOU DIDN‚ÄôT! THEN SHE TRIED TO HELP?????????? AM I SUPPOSED TO TRUST DESPINA ORR???? But then in the epilogue, the baby was born and all was forgiven.<br>I am still reeling from the ride and that the series is done so soon. So I shall leave you with one more beautiful quote from this lovely story.<br><b><br>‚ÄúIn the end, there is only time for love.‚Äù<br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>THIS BOOK HAD MY EYES FILLING WITH TEARS NEAR THE END THEN BOOM NEXT CHAPTER, tears were turned into bliss at a somewhat happy ending.<br>Full review to come.<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>I am SUPER excited to start this book, BUT I WOULD LIKE TO EXPRESS MY GRATITUDE TO WHOEVER DESIGNED THIS SERIES COVERS! THEY ARE EXQUISITE AND I'M FEELING THEM <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477587319ra/20969135.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> YAS</b></p></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039633955" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2039633955?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780147513861" href="/book/show/31521391-the-rose-the-dagger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=almost-great">almost-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039633955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2599325623820558327"><b> 3.5 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>‚ÄúIt was because they were two parts of a whole. He did not belong to her. And she did not belong to him. It was never about belonging to someone. It was about belonging together.‚Äù </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Just like the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816628283' rel='nofollow noopener'>first book,</a> I‚Äôm conflicted. There were parts I <i>loved</i> and parts I thought were very unnecessary. <br/><br/><b>Pros:</b><br/><br/>Surprisingly, I really loved the relationship between Shazi and Khalid. In the first book, I had a lot of issues with it ethically, and while those issues are still kind of there, t</span>
  <span id="freeText2599325623820558327" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 Stars<br /><br />Overview: </b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>‚ÄúIt was because they were two parts of a whole. He did not belong to her. And she did not belong to him. It was never about belonging to someone. It was about belonging together.‚Äù </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Just like the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816628283" rel="nofollow noopener">first book,</a> I‚Äôm conflicted. There were parts I <i>loved</i> and parts I thought were very unnecessary. <br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />Surprisingly, I really loved the relationship between Shazi and Khalid. In the first book, I had a lot of issues with it ethically, and while those issues are still kind of there, their relationship as a whole seems much more mature. They both love with this <i>intensity</i> and it was kind of beautiful how fiercely protective they both were.<br /><br />The fantasy element was explored in more depth here, and was a lot of fun!<br /><br />Familial relationships are often one of my favorites, and I loved the focus on Shazi‚Äôs sister, Irsa. Especially since her strength is quieter (but no less important!) than Shazi‚Äôs. <br /><br />I just really enjoyed the writing style? It seemed more balanced-- painting beautiful scenes, while still progressing the narrative. Pacing worked well, as there's a fine thread of tension weaved throughout the entire story. <br /><br />There‚Äôs something really impactful about three completely different women coming together for an ending that utilized their unique strengths.<br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />I don‚Äôt like the way things wrapped up for Shazi‚Äôs dad. That was a lot of drama in the last ten pages that didn‚Äôt amount to much. <br /><br />Resolution for Khalid‚Äôs curse was really underwhelming? The plot shifted and focused instead on the impending war, which was interesting, but the entire first book was about this curse? <br /><br />Though I liked it more this round, I still feel there are some weird undertones in Shazi/Khalid‚Äôs whole relationship (which are addressed) and I often wondered <i>why</i> they fell for each other in the first place. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion:</b><br /><br />Idk man. I definitely enjoyed it, but I didn't <i>love</i> it. üåπüó°</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sSRUCR0zWBQmTUlUSxRIBTuBMkDE8vFEKRS+g0WpN8vumUPsY//oxM8aF1MHy6Yix+cf8v+/RIHlbKVbuZrmUA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('91GCKrKC2CyvHphi3a4S4CNTdyOHqHZlrtsTgRj62eio7JXPzE5o/EZJxmWRcfzH3zVakbzlw6BiowhZ5MkIcw==')})
  }

When sixteen-year-old Shahrzad\'s dearest friend falls victim to Khalid, Shahrzad vows vengeance and volunteers to be his next bride. Shahrzad is determined not only to stay alive, but to end the caliph\'s reign of terror once and for all.\n\nNight after night, Shahrzad beguiles Khalid, weaving stories that enchant, ensuring her survival, though she knows each dawn could be her last. Incredibly, Shahrzad finds herself falling in love. How is this possible? It\'s an unforgivable betrayal. Still, Shahrzad has come to understand all is not as it seems in this palace of marble and stone. She resolves to uncover whatever secrets lurk and, despite her love, be ready to take Khalid\'s life as retribution for the many lives he\'s stolen.
